id=3D\"School\" /></a>=0A</div>=0A<div id=\n=3D\"editorial\">=0A  <h1>History</h1>=0A  <p class=3D\"historybodytext\">Born =\nto a wealthy and privileged family in 1889, in one of the most exclusive co=\nmmunities in American history, Tuxedo Park, Dorothy Draper was the first to=\n =E2=80=9Cprofessionalize=E2=80=9D the interior design industry by establis=\nhing, in 1923, the first interior design company in the United States, some=\nthing that until then was unheard of, and also at a time when it was consid=\nered daring for a woman to go into business for herself.</p><br />=0A  <p c=\nlass=3D\"historybodytext\">As Carleton Varney writes in the biography of his =\nmentor, The Draper Touch, she revolutionized the concept of =E2=80=9Cdesign=\n=E2=80=9D by breaking away from the historical =E2=80=9Cperiod room=E2=80=\n=9D styles that dominated the work of her predecessors and contemporaries. =\nAs an artist she was a modern, one of the first decorators of the breed, an=\nd a pioneer. She invented =E2=80=9CModern Baroque=E2=80=9D, a style that ha=\nd particular application to large public spaces and modern architecture. Sh=\ne craved public space, the canvas on which she did her most inspired work (=\n e.g. the restaurant at the Metropolitan Museum of Art, New York, nicknamed=\n =E2=80=9CThe Dorotheum=E2=80=9D). To Dorothy, public space represented a p=\nlace for people to come and feel elevated in the presence of great beauty, =\nwhere the senses could look and feel and absorb the meaning of a quality li=\nfe. She used vibrant, =E2=80=9Csplashy=E2=80=9D colors in never-before-seen=\n combinations, such as aubergine and pink with a =E2=80=9Csplash=E2=80=9D o=\nf chartreuse and a touch of turquoise blue, or, one of her favorite combina=\ntions - =E2=80=9Cdull=E2=80=9D white and =E2=80=9Cshiny=E2=80=9D black. Her=\n signature =E2=80=9Ccabbage rose=E2=80=9D chintz, paired with bold stripes;=\n her elaborate and ornate plaster designs and moldings - over doors, on wal=\nls and ceilings; her black and white checkered floors (The Quitandinah Pala=\nce & Casino Resort, Petropolis, Brazil); her massive, paneled, lacquered do=\nors (Arrowhead Springs Hotel, California), some framed with bolection (Hamp=\nshire House, New York) or with elaborate plaster or intricate mirror frames=\n (Camellia House, Drake Hotel, Chicago) =E2=80=93 all contributed to dramat=\nic design often referred to as =E2=80=9Cthe Draper touch=E2=80=9D.</p>=0A  =\n<br />=0A  <p class=3D\"historybodytext\">Her confidence, as much as her tast=\ne, gave her the ability to take control of a hotel project in all aspects o=\nf design =E2=80=93 right down to the designs for menus, matchbook covers an=\nd the staff uniforms. Her dictum was =E2=80=9Cif it looks right, it is righ=\nt=E2=80=9D.</p>=0A  <br />=0A  <p class=3D\"historybodytext\"><img src=3D\"Pic=\ns/History/Greebrier.jpg\" alt=3D\"The Garden Gallery\" class=3D\"historypic\" />=\nThe Greenbrier Hotel, White Sulphur Springs,  West Virginia</p>=0A  <br />=\n=0A  <p class=3D\"historybodytext\">In her day, Dorothy was the prima donna o=\nf the decorating business =E2=80=93 her name was synonymous with decorating=\n. She gave decorating advice in her regular column for Good Housekeeping Ma=\ngazine, designed fabric lines for Schumacher, furniture for Ficks Reed, Her=\nitage and, other than her hotel and restaurant decors, she also designed th=\neaters, department stores, commercial establishments, private corporate off=\nices, the interiors of jet planes (Convair & TWA) , automobiles (she did a =\n=E2=80=9Cline=E2=80=9D for Packard and Chrysler in the 1950=E2=80=99s =E2=\n=80=93 including a pink polka dot truck!) =E2=80=93 even packaging for the =\ncosmetics firm of Dorothy Gray =E2=80=93 on top of her residential designs =\nfor the houses and apartments of prominent and very wealthy society figures=\n. She also designed her very own exclusive fabrics for her clients =E2=80=\n=93 such as her Romance & Rhododendrons and Fudge Apron which she used at t=\nhe Greenbrier. Much of her work survives to this day, in the lobbies of apa=\nrtment buildings, hotels (The Carlyle in New York and Hampshire House until=\n recently) and of course, the legendary Greenbrier in White Sulphur Springs=\n, West Virginia, specifically in The Victorian Writing Room =E2=80=93 once =\ncalled the most photographed room in the United States).</p><br />=0A  <p c=\nlass=3D\"historybodytext\">The year 2006 was a milestone in the American inte=\nrior design industry - for it was in that year that the legendary Dorothy D=\nraper, a doyenne of the interior design industry of the 20th Century, was h=\nonored in a restrospective exhibition of her work by the Museum of the City=\n of New York =E2=80=93 the first time that such an honor was given to an in=\nterior designer. It was enormously successful, and it is estimated that mor=\ne than 300,000 people attended over a period of six months. The exhibit con=\ntinued to the Woman=E2=80=99s Museum in Fair Park (Dallas, Texas) where aga=\nin it spurred much interest. In February 2008 it will continue on to the Mu=\nseum of Art in Fort Lauderdale, Florida =E2=80=93 such is the interest of t=\nhis phenomenal giant in the design industry.</p>=0A  <br /><br /><br /><br =\n/><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><=\nbr /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />=0A</div>=0A=0A<div id=3D\"ri=\nghtcolumn\"><img src=3D\"Pics/History/DorothyDraper.gif\" alt=3D\"Dorothy Drape=\nr\" /></div>=0A<div id=3D\"rightcolumn\"><img src=3D\"http://ecx.images-amazon.=\ncom/images/I/51QfUgfKHPL._SL500_AA300_.jpg\" alt=3D\"Mr. Color\" />=0A<p class=\n=3D\"historypromotext\">Carleton Varney is \"Mr. Color,\" known for his inventi=\nve use of unexpected color combinations and for creating bright, happy inte=\nriors. id=3D\"School\" /></a>=0A</div>=0A=\n<br />=0A<div id=3D\"editorial\">=0A  <h1>Carleton Varney</h1>=0A  <p class=\n=3D\"bodytext\">=0A  =0ACarleton Varney - one of America's best known interio=\nr designers - is the president/owner of Dorothy Draper & Co. Inc., located =\nin New York City.  It is one of the oldest established interior design firm=\ns in the United States and is named after the founder of the company, Dorot=\nhy Draper, a doyenne of interior design in the United States from the 1920'=\ns to the 1960's.  The Varney design philosophy stresses=E2=80=A6\"the use of=\n bright colors and the rejection of all that is impractical, uncomfortable =\nand drab\".  In embracing this practice, he continues the tradition of Dorot=\nhy Draper, by being associated with the adventurous use of vibrant colors, =\nfloral patterns and bold contrasts.<br /><br />=0A=0ACarleton Varney's impr=\nessive roster of clients includes superstars from the worlds of entertainme=\nnt, fashion and business.  He is associated with the restoration and decora=\ntion of countless hotels and resorts in Europe, Asia, the Caribbean, and th=\ne United States.  Among them:  Dromoland and Ashford Castles, and Adare Man=\nor in Ireland; The Westbury Hotel, London and Brussels;  The Breakers and t=\nhe Brazilian Court, Palm Beach (Florida); The Waldorf Towers, New York City=\n;  The Copley Plaza, Boston, (Massachusetts);  The Grand Hotel, Mackinac Is=\nland (Michigan); The Greenbrier Hotel & Casino, White Sulphur Springs (West=\n Virginia) and the Greenbrier West Village Resort (Japan);  The Mount Washi=\nngton Hotel, New Hampshire; The Stoneleigh Hotel, Dallas, Texas; Peter Isla=\nnd Resort Hotel, British Virgin Islands, and Villa Madeleine, St. Croix, U.=\nS. Virgin Islands.   He decorated the Governor's Mansion in West Virginia a=\nnd was involved in the decoration of the U.S Ambassador=E2=80=99s Residence=\n  in Tokyo, Japan.  He restored and redecorated the Official Vice President=\n's Residence in Washington D.C. and was the color consultant for the Carter=\n Presidential Library and the consultant for several functions, parties and=\n State Dinners for visiting dignitaries at the White House.  Current projec=\nts include the decoration of a residence in Indian Wells, California, and a=\n sprawling residence in San Antonio, Texas.  In the planning stage are the =\ninteriors of the Greenbrier Presidential Express, to be launched in the nea=\nr future, which will take passengers from Washington D.C. to the Greenbrier=\n Resort in White Sulphur Springs, West Virginia.  It will echo the magical =\ninteriors of its destination property, The Greenbrier.<br /><br />=0A=0AIn =\naddition to the decoration of numerous private residences, the company has =\nalso been associated with the decoration of cruise ship and private plane i=\nnteriors.  Carleton Varney was the curator of the former presidential yacht=\n, the USS \"Sequoia\".  In 2008 he also designed the Architectural Digest Gre=\nen Room for the Academy Awards celebration at the Kodak Theatre, in Los Ang=\neles.<br /><br />=0A=0AMr. Varney's versatility in design can be seen in th=\ne wide range of products that bear his mark, ranging from dinnerware, cryst=\nal, scarves, and he has designed a line of furniture for the =0ARomweber an=\nd Kindel Furniture companies as well as for Ficks Reed.  His fabric designs=\n, launched under the names <b>Carleton V Ltd.</b> (New York) and <b>Carleto=\nn Varney by the yard</b> (Palm Beach, Florida) grace the rooms of some of A=\nmerica's most beautiful resorts and homes.  He also appears regularly on th=\ne HSN television program =E2=80=9CLive Vividly - Carleton Varney=E2=80=9D f=\neaturing home d=C3=A9cor items of his designs.<br /><br />=0A=0ACarleton Va=\nrney also writes a weekly decorating column, \"Your Family Decorator\" in the=\n Palm Beach Daily News =E2=80=93 also known as =E2=80=9CThe Shiny Sheet=E2=\n=80=9D.  He is the author of numerous books, mostly on decoration and inter=\nior design, but he has also written a biography of Dorothy Draper entitled =\n<b>The Draper Touch</b>.  He has penned two novels,  <b>Kiss the Hibiscus G=\nood Night</b> and <b>The Decorator</b>.  In conjunction with the museum exh=\nibitions on the <i>High Style of Dorothy Draper</i> at the Museum of the Ci=\nty of New York, The Women=E2=80=99s Museum in Dallas, Texas and the Museum =\nof Art in Fort Lauderdale, Florida,  (2006-2008) he published the book, <b>=\nIn The Pink =E2=80=93 Dorothy Draper, America=E2=80=99s most Fabulous Decor=\nator</b>.  He has also published =E2=80=93 Houses in My Heart -  a book tha=\nt features his favorite design projects during the course of his career.  H=\nis latest book =E2=80=93entitled <b>Mr. Color</b> - features his latest com=\nmissions, using his trademark color palate on his imaginative interiors.<br=\n /><br />=0A=0AA native son of Lynn, Massachusetts, he was educated at Ober=\nlin College, Ohio, where he obtained his Bachelors of Arts degree - and the=\n University of Madrid, Spain.  He obtained his Master of Arts degree at New=\n York University.  He also holds an honorary doctorate from the University =\nof Charleston, West Virginia, and founded the Carleton Varney School of Art=\n & Design in that institution.  <i>Architectural Digest</i>, in its January=\n 2005 edition, named him as one of the 30 =E2=80=9C<i>Deans of American Des=\nign</i>=E2=80=9D.<br /><br />=0A=0ACarleton Varney is the father of three s=\nons.<br /><br /><br />=0A=0A  =0A  =0A  =0A  <!--Carleton Varney, one of Am=\nerica=E2=80=99s best known interior designers, is associated with the resto=\nration and decoration of countless hotels and resorts all over the world, a=\nmong them: Dromoland and Ashford Castles in Ireland; The Waldorf Towers and=\n Plaza Hotel in New York; Grand Hotel on Mackinac Island (Michigan) ; The B=\nreakers in Palm Beach and the Greenbrier in West Virginia. <div id=3D\"personnelthumb\"><img alt=3D\"Carleton =\nVarney\" src =3D\"../Pics/Personnel/Carleton-Varney.jpg\" ></div> =0A  <p clas=\ns=3D\"bodytext\">Carleton Varney, one of America's best known interior design=\ners, is associated with the restoration and decoration of countless hotels =\nand resorts all over the world, among them: =0AAdare Manor,  Dromoland and =\nAshford Castles in Ireland; The Waldorf Towers and Plaza Hotel in New York;=\n  Grand Hotel on Mackinac Island (Michigan) ; The Breakers in Palm=0ABeach =\n(Florida), and the Greenbrier in White Sulphur Springs, (West Virginia).  I=\nn years past he was the design consultant to the Carter Presidential Librar=\ny and for numerous State functions at the White House.  He also restored an=\nd redecorated the Official Vice President's Residence in Washington D.C., t=\nhe Governor's Mansion in West Virginia, and the U.S. Ambassador's residence=\n in Tokyo, Japan.<br ><br >=0A=0A His versatility in design can be seen in =\nthe wide range of products that have borne his mark, ranging from furniture=\n, lamps, dinner-ware, crystal and linen  designs. His own line of fabric de=\nsigns, launched under thename Carleton V Ltd.,  and Carleton Varney by the =\nyard, grace the private residences of his impressive roster of clients whic=\nh include superstars from =0Athe worlds of entertainment, fashion and  busi=\nness. Just introduced to  the market is a line of furniture based on Doroth=\ny Draper designs, for Ficks Reed and also ready to launch is a new Errol Fl=\nynn Collection (a joint collaboration between Carleton Varney and the actor=\n's wife, Patrice Wymore Flynn) for the Kindel Furniture Company; a collecti=\non inspired by the movie star's furniture on his Jamaica estate.<br ><br >=\n=0A=0A Recent projects include a just completed apartment in Washington D.C=\n., with a distinctly 'Moroccan' flavor for a prominent business couple, a v=\nast New York Fifth Avenue apartment,a summer house in Southampton, N.Y. and=\n an Addison Mizner designed residence in Palm Beach for celebrity clients f=\nrom the theater  world. Other recent projects include two residences in Cal=\nifornia (Palm Springs &amp; Lake Arrowhead), and two houses on the island o=\nf St. Croix in the U.S. Virgin Islands. Two of his current projects include=\n a 21,000 sq. ft. residence on Lake Michigan with a separate 6,000 sq. ft. =\nboat house on the lake  and a vast residence in Jackson Hole,  Wyoming. Jus=\nt finished are the penthouse suites at the Stoneleigh Hotel in Dallas,  Tex=\nas. Two other recent commercial projects include,  an office building in Ch=\narleston, West Virginia, and a luxurious senior living complex in Denver,  =\nColorado. In February 2008, he decorated the famous Architectural Digest Gr=\neen Room at the 80th Academy Awards ceremony at the Kodak Theatre in Los An=\ngeles, in which all the movie stars and award presenters gather before they=\n go on  stage. In its beginning stages, is perhaps one of his most prestigi=\nous assignments; the interior design of the Royal Palace in Vilnius, Lithua=\nnia, which is currently being restored to its original splendor.<br ><br >=\n=0A=0AHe is the president of Dorothy Draper &amp; Co. Inc. (New York), one =\nof the oldest established interior design firms in the United States, named=\n after the founder of the company who was one of the doyenes of interior de=\nsign from the 1920's to the 1960's and who was honored by the Museum of the=\n City of New York in 2006 in a very successful retrospective exhibition of =\nher work -  (the exhibition continued on to The Women's Museum in Dallas, T=\nexas, in 2007, and then on to the Museum of Art in Fort Lauderdale, Florida=\n until June 2008).<br ><br >=0A=0A  Carleton Varney has penned a biography =\non Dorothy Draper entitled The Draper Touch&nbsp;: The High Life and High S=\ntyle of Dorothy  Draper. His pictorial book on Dorothy Draper, In The Pink =\n- Dorothy Draper - Americas's most fabulous Decorator, published concurrent=\nly with the museum exhibitions, is filled with countless photographs of her=\n work, taken from the archives of Dorothy Draper &amp; Company and includes=\n many photographs that have never been published  before. Carleton Varney i=\ns also a well known syndicated newspaper columnist and author of numerous b=\nooks, most on design, but also including two novels: Kiss the Hibiscus Good=\n Night and The Decorator and an autobiography entitled There's No Place Lik=\ne Home.  His latest book  - Houses in my Heart (An International Decorator'=\ns Colorful Journey)  is published by Pointed Leaf Press..  It is a lavishly=\n illustrated book featuring many of his interior design projects throughout=\n his career.<br ><br >=0A=0A Carleton Varney's design philosophy stresses t=\nhe use of bright colors and the rejection of all that is impractical, uncom=\nfortable and  drab. In embracing this practice, he continues the tradition =\nof Dorothy Draper by being associated with the imaginative use of vibrant c=\nolors, floral patterns and bold contrasts; a legacy that is reflected, not =\nonly in his interior designs, but also, most notably, in his fabric and sca=\nrf designs.<br ><br >=0A=0A<span class=3D\"subheading\">Professional Affiliat=\nion:</span>\tMember
